---
layout: "post"
title: "HoTT exercises"
date: "2018-04-08"
categories: type-theory
toc: true
---

This is a self-contained version of some solutions for HoTT-Book's exercises.
The idea is to unpackage all as long as possible to get a better understanding.
Many changes can appear running this experiment. Solutions are
type-checked as a whole using Agda v2.5.3.

## Requirements

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Agda has a pragma to work with HoTT:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="516" class="Symbol">{-#</a> <a id="520" class="Keyword">OPTIONS</a> <a id="528" class="Option">--without-K</a> <a id="540" class="Symbol">#-}</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Equality type definition also called Identity type:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="703" class="Keyword">infix</a> <a id="709" class="Number">4</a> <a id="711" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">_≡_</a>

## Chapter 1

### Exercise 1.1

{: .exercise}
  Given functions $$f : A \to B$$ and $$g:B\to C$$, define
  their composite $$ g\circ f:A\to C$$.
  Show that we have $$h \circ (g\circ f) \equiv (h\circ g)\circ f$$.


We define the composition operation in Agda as follows.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="_∘_" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%88%98_" class="Function Operator">_∘_</a> <a id="2117" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2119" class="Symbol">∀</a> <a id="2121" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="2122" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2122" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="2124" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2124" class="Bound">j</a> <a id="2126" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2126" class="Bound">k</a><a id="2127" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="2129" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="2130" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2130" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="2132" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2134" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2138" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2122" class="Bound">i</a><a id="2139" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="2141" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2141" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="2143" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2145" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2149" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2124" class="Bound">j</a><a id="2150" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="2152" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2152" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="2154" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="2156" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="2160" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2126" class="Bound">k</a><a id="2161" class="Symbol">}</a>
    <a id="2167" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2169" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="2170" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2141" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="2172" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="2174" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#2152" class="Bound">C</a><a id="2175" class="Symbol">)</a>

Then, the `∘-assoc` shows us that associativity of this composition holds.

### Exercise 1.2

<div class="exercise">
Derive the recursion principle for products $$\mathsf{rec}_{A\times B}$$
using only the projections, and verify that the definitional equalities
are valid. Do the same for $$\Sigma$$-types.
</div>

To solve this problem we need to know:

  - The recursion principle for Σ-types:

    <p class="equation">
    $$ \mathsf{rec}_{ A \times B}
      : \prod\limits_{C : \mathcal{U}} (A \to B \to C) → A \times B \to C.
    $$
    </p>

  - The recursion principle for Σ-types:

    <p class="equation">
    $$ \mathsf{rec}_{\sum\limits_{(x : A) } B(x)}
      : \prod\limits_{(C : U)} (\Pi_{(x : A)} B(x) \rightarrow C) \rightarrow
        \sum_{(x : A)} B(x) \rightarrow C
    $$
    </p>

<div class="proof" id="proof-1.2">
Proof.<br/>
For products:<br/>
If we have the projections,
$$\mathsf{proj}_1 : A \times B \to \mathsf{A}$$ and $$\mathsf{proj}_2 : A \times B \to \mathsf{B}$$,
then $$\mathsf{rec}_2$$ is another inhabitant where

<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
&\mathsf{rec}_1 : \prod\limits_{C : \mathcal{U}} (A \to B \to C) \to A \times B \to C\\
&\mathsf{rec}_1~C~g~c~:\equiv~g~(\mathsf{proj}_1 c,~\mathsf{proj}_2 c).
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
By reflexivity, we prove the equality between $$\mathsf{rec}_{ A \times B}$$ and $$\mathsf{rec}_1$$.
<br/>
<br/>
For sums:<br/>
The projections are $$\mathsf{proj}_1 : \sum_{x : A}  Bx \to \mathsf{A}$$ and
$$\mathsf{proj}_2 :  \prod_{(p : \sum_{x : A}  Bx)} \to \mathsf{B} (\mathsf{proj}_1 p)$$.<br/>
By using these projections, we got another recursor defined as follows:
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{aling*}
&\mathsf{rec}_2 : \prod\limits_{C : \mathcal{U}}  (\prod_{x : A} Bx \to C) \to \sum\limits_{x : A} B x \to C\\
&\mathsf{rec}_2~C~g~c~=~g~(\mathsf{proj}_1 c)~(\mathsf{proj}_2 c)
\end{align*}
$$
</p>

By reflexivity, we prove the equality between $$\mathsf{rec}_{\sum\limits_{(x : A) } B(x)}$$ and $$\mathsf{rec}_2$$.
</div>

In Agda.<br>

Let's add some machinery to handle levels of the universe needed for
the following exercises including this one:

  <a id="5057" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="5062" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3" class="Module">Σ</a> <a id="5064" class="Keyword">public</a>
<a id="5071" class="Comment">-- _,_ : (proj₁ : A) → B proj₁ → Σ A B.</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Its recursor with a function $$g : \prod_{(x : A)} B(x)\rightarrow C$$
that we provide.

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

On the other hand, the product type is just a particular case of the sigma type
when the codomain is not dependent, as we can see next by omitting the argument
in `(λ _ → B)`.

Its recursor with a function $$g : A \rightarrow B \rightarrow C$$ that we provide.

### Exercise 1.3

<p class="exercise">
Derive the induction principle for products $$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B}$$,
using only the projections and the propositional uniqueness principle
$$\mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}$$.
Verify that the definitional equalities are valid.
</p>

To solve this problem, recall the uniqueness principle (Pp. 29. HoTT-Book)

- The **propositional uniqueness principle** says that
every element of $$A\times B$$ is equal to a pair.

<p class="equation">
  $$ \mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}
     : \prod_{(x : A \times B)} ((\mathsf{proj}_{1}(x) , \mathsf{proj}_{2}(x))
       \equiv_{A\times B} x).
  $$
</p>

Product type definition using `data`:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="6943" class="Comment">-- this would be trivial in agda due to definitional η for records</a>
<a id="7010" class="Comment">-- so Capriotti defined a product type without η:</a>

  <a id="7944" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Fun%E2%82%82.pair%3D" class="Function">pair=</a> <a id="7950" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="7955" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a> <a id="7960" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="7962" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

The induction principle for the product type:

<p class="equation">
$$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B} : \prod\limits_{C : A \times B \to \mathcal{U}}
  \left( \prod\limits_{x:A}\ \prod\limits_{y:B}\ \,C( (x,y) ) \right)
  \to \prod\limits_{x:A \times B}\ \,C(x)
$$
</p>

        <a id="8416" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8418" class="Symbol">((</a><a id="8420" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8420" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8422" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8424" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8276" class="Bound">A</a><a id="8425" class="Symbol">)(</a><a id="8427" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8427" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="8429" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8431" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8287" class="Bound">B</a><a id="8432" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8434" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8436" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8389" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="8438" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8439" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8420" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8441" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="8443" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8427" class="Bound">y</a><a id="8444" class="Symbol">))</a>
        <a id="8455" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8457" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="8458" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8458" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8460" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="8462" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8276" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="8464" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Def%E2%82%82._%C3%97_" class="Datatype Operator">×</a> <a id="8466" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8287" class="Bound">B</a><a id="8467" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="8469" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="8471" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8389" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="8473" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8458" class="Bound">x</a>

  <a id="8677" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%C3%97-Ind%E2%82%82.ind-%CE%B2" class="Function">ind-β</a> <a id="8683" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8683" class="Bound">C</a> <a id="8685" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8685" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="8687" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8687" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="8689" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#8689" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="8691" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="8693" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

<p class="exercise">
Generalize $$\mathsf{uniq}_{A\times B}$$ to Σ-types, and do the same for
$$\Sigma$$-types, i.e. show induction and verify the definitional equality
is valid.
</p>

Σ-type definition using `data`:

### Exercise 1.4

<div class="exercise">
Assuming as given only the <em>iterator</em> for natural numbers
<p class="equation">
$$\mathsf{ite} : \prod\limits_{C:\mathcal{U}} C \to (C \to C) \to \mathbb{N} \to C $$
</p>
with the defining equations
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,0)               &\equiv c_0, \\
\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,\mathsf{suc}(n)) &\equiv c_s(\mathsf{ite}(C,c_0,c_s,n)),
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
derive a function having the type of the recursor $$\mathsf{rec}$$.
Show that the defining equations of the recursor hold propositionally for this
function, using the induction principle for $$\mathbb{N}$$.
</div>

To solve this problem, let us define the recursor and also the induction principle
for natural numbers. (See more details about these functions in
[Induction on Natural Numbers]({% post_url 2018-02-12-induction-on-natural-numbers %})).

Now, we define the iterator following the equations above:

Then, we now can define the recursor using this `ite` by iterating over the type
`ℕ × C` (*reloading recursion*?).

           <a id="11860" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#11733" class="Bound">n</a><a id="11861" class="Symbol">)</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Now, we need to establish the propositional equality between these two
definitions of recursor, i.e, between `rec` and `rec₂`. Let's use
induction to prove that.

### Exercise 1.5

<div class="exercise">

Show that if we define

  $$A+B :\equiv \sum\limits_{(x : \mathbbbold{2})} \mathsf{rec}_{\mathbbbold{2}} (\mathcal{U}, A , B, x),$$

then we can give a definition of $$\ind\limits_{A + B}$$ for which the
definitional equalities holds.

</div>

To solve this problem, let us introduce the $$\mathcal{2}$$ type, that is, the
type with two constructors also called **Bool**. The constructors are also called
false and true respectively.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="13301" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="𝟚-Def₁" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81" class="Module">𝟚-Def₁</a> <a id="13315" class="Keyword">where</a>

  <a id="13324" class="Keyword">data</a> <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a> <a id="13331" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13333" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="13337" class="Keyword">where</a>
    <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚.𝟘" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%98" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟘</a> <a id="13349" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13351" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a>
    <a id="𝟚-Def₁.𝟚.𝟙" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%99" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟙</a> <a id="13359" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="13361" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A" class="Datatype">𝟚</a>{% endraw %}</pre>


With the recursor:

  <a id="13545" class="Comment">-- rec is the same if_then_else</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

and its induction principle:

The we define the **coproduct** $$A+B$$ as follows:

Now, let's try to define the recursor for this coproduct, and later,
we'll try the dependent version of it to complete the exercise.

      <a id="14544" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="14546" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14547" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14499" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="14549" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="14551" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14511" class="Bound">C</a><a id="14552" class="Symbol">)</a>
      <a id="14560" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="14562" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14497" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="14564" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%2B-Def%E2%82%81._%2B_" class="Function Operator">+</a> <a id="14566" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14499" class="Bound">B</a> <a id="14568" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="14570" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14511" class="Bound">C</a>
  <a id="14574" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%2B-Rec%E2%82%81.rec" class="Function">rec</a> <a id="14578" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14578" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="14580" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14580" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="14582" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14583" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%98" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟘</a> <a id="14585" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="14587" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14587" class="Bound">a</a><a id="14588" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="14590" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="14592" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14578" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="14594" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14587" class="Bound">a</a>
  <a id="14598" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%2B-Rec%E2%82%81.rec" class="Function">rec</a> <a id="14602" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14602" class="Bound">f</a> <a id="14604" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14604" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="14606" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="14607" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%F0%9D%9F%9A-Def%E2%82%81.%F0%9D%9F%9A.%F0%9D%9F%99" class="InductiveConstructor">𝟙</a> <a id="14609" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Def%E2%82%81.%CE%A3._%2C_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">,</a> <a id="14611" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14611" class="Bound">b</a><a id="14612" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="14614" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="14616" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14604" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="14618" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#14611" class="Bound">b</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

Notice how the recursor of the coproduct matches with the elimination
rule of the disjunction conective also called *case analysis*. That's follows from the
[**propositions-as-types**](https://ncatlab.org/nlab/show/propositions+as+types).

![path](/assets/latexit-images/disj-elimination.png)

Finally, the induction principle for the coproduct:

### Exercise 1.6

<div class="exercise" id="ex-1.6">
Show that if we define $$A \times B :≡ \prod_{x:\mathbf{2}}\mathsf{rec}_{\mathbf{2}}\ (\mathcal{U}\, A\, B\, x)$$,
then we can give a definition of $$\mathsf{ind}_{A\times B}$$ for which the definitional
equalities propositionally (i.e. using equality types).
</div>

          <a id="17395" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#17395" class="Function">right-inverse</a> <a id="17409" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17411" class="Symbol">∀</a> <a id="17413" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="17414" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#17414" class="Bound">i</a><a id="17415" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="17417" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#17417" class="Bound">X</a> <a id="17419" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17421" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a> <a id="17425" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#17414" class="Bound">i</a><a id="17426" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="17428" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#17428" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="17430" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#17430" class="Bound">y</a> <a id="17432" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17434" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#17417" class="Bound">X</a><a id="17435" class="Symbol">}</a>
                        <a id="17461" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="17463" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="17464" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#17464" class="Bound">p</a> <a id="17466" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="17468" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#17428" class="Bound">x</a> <a id="17470" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="17472" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#17430" class="Bound">y</a><a id="17473" class="Symbol">)</a>
                        <a id="17499" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="17501" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="17502" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#sym" class="Function">sym</a> <a id="17506" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#17464" class="Bound">p</a><a id="17507" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="17509" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%C2%B7_" class="Function Operator">·</a> <a id="17511" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#17464" class="Bound">p</a> <a id="17513" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="17515" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_.refl" class="InductiveConstructor">refl</a>

### Exercise 1.8

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.8">

Define multiplication and exponentiation using $$\mathsf{rec}{\mathbb{N}}$$.
Verify that $$(\mathbb{N},+,0,\times,1)$$ is a semiring using only
$$\ind{\mathbb{N}}$$.

</div>


<div class="proof" markdown="1">
Solution.<br/>
Operation definitions:

id="18154" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="18156" class="Symbol">(λ</a> <a id="18159" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#18159" class="Bound">n</a> <a id="18161" class="Bound">m</a> <a id="18165" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="18167" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#Ex1-8.multi" class="Function">multi</a> <a id="18173" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#18163" class="Bound">m</a> <a id="18175" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="18176" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#18161" class="Bound">g</a> <a id="18178" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#18163" class="Bound">m</a><a id="18179" class="Symbol">))</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

On the other hand, a **semiring** is a type? together with two binary operators S(+,*) satisfying the following conditions:

1. Additive associativity: $$\prod_{a,b,c : S} (a+b)+c=a+(b+c)$$.

2. Additive commutativity: $$\prod_{a,b : S}  a+b=b+a$$.

3. Multiplicative associativity: $$\prod_{a,b,c : S} (a*b)*c=a*(b*c)$$.

4. Left and right distributivity:

$$\prod_{a,b,c : S} a*(b+c)=(a*b)+(a*c)\text{  and  } \prod_{a,b,c : S} (b+c)*a=(b*a)+(c*a).$$

</div>

### Exercise 1.9

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.9">

Define the type family $$\mathsf{Fin} : \mathbb{N} \to \mathcal{U}$$ mentioned
at the end of Section 1.3, and the dependent function $$\mathsf{fmax} :
\prod_{n:\mathbb{N}} \mathsf{Fin}(n+1)$$ mentioned in Section 1.4.
</div>

### Exercise 1.11

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.11">
Show that for any type $$A$$, we have $$\neg\neg\neg A \to \neg A$$.
</div>

A propositional logic proof using [Agda-Prop](http://github.com/jonaprieto/agda-prop)
library:

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="20108" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="Ex1-11" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#Ex1-11" class="Module">Ex1-11</a> <a id="20122" class="Keyword">where</a>
  <a id="20130" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="20135" class="Keyword">import</a> <a id="20142" href="Data.PropFormula.html" class="Module">Data.PropFormula</a> <a id="20159" class="Number">1</a>

  <a id="Ex1-11.proof" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#Ex1-11.proof" class="Function">proof</a> <a id="20170" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="20172" class="Symbol">∀</a> <a id="20174" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="20175" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20175" class="Bound">Γ</a><a id="20176" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="20178" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="20179" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20179" class="Bound">A</a><a id="20180" class="Symbol">}</a>
        <a id="20190" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="20192" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20175" class="Bound">Γ</a> <a id="20194" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#_%E2%8A%A2_" class="Datatype Operator">⊢</a> <a id="20196" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20198" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20200" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20202" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20179" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="20204" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#_%E2%8A%83_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">⊃</a> <a id="20206" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20208" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20179" class="Bound">A</a>

          <a id="20264" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20265" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC-elim" class="InductiveConstructor">¬-elim</a>
              <a id="20286" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20287" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#weaken" class="InductiveConstructor">weaken</a> <a id="20294" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20222" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="20296" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20297" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#assume" class="InductiveConstructor">assume</a> <a id="20304" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="20305" class="Argument">Γ</a> <a id="20307" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="20309" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20219" class="Bound">Γ</a><a id="20310" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="20312" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20313" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20315" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20316" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20318" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20319" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20321" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20222" class="Bound">A</a><a id="20322" class="Symbol">)))))</a>
              <a id="20342" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20343" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC-intro" class="InductiveConstructor">¬-intro</a>
                <a id="20367" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20368" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC-elim" class="InductiveConstructor">¬-elim</a>
                  <a id="20393" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20394" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#assume" class="InductiveConstructor">assume</a> <a id="20401" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="20402" class="Argument">Γ</a> <a id="20404" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="20406" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20219" class="Bound">Γ</a> <a id="20408" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#_%2C_" class="Function Operator">,</a> <a id="20410" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20412" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20414" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20416" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20222" class="Bound">A</a> <a id="20418" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#_%2C_" class="Function Operator">,</a> <a id="20420" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20222" class="Bound">A</a><a id="20421" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="20423" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20424" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20426" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20222" class="Bound">A</a><a id="20427" class="Symbol">))</a>
                  <a id="20448" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20449" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#weaken" class="InductiveConstructor">weaken</a> <a id="20456" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20457" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20459" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20222" class="Bound">A</a><a id="20460" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="20462" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20463" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#assume" class="InductiveConstructor">assume</a> <a id="20470" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="20471" class="Argument">Γ</a> <a id="20473" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="20475" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20219" class="Bound">Γ</a> <a id="20477" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#_%2C_" class="Function Operator">,</a> <a id="20479" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20481" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20483" href="Data.PropFormula.Syntax.html#%C2%AC_" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">¬</a> <a id="20485" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20222" class="Bound">A</a><a id="20486" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="20488" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20222" class="Bound">A</a><a id="20489" class="Symbol">))))))</a>{% endraw %}</pre>

In type theory, the term is:

$$
λ (x : ((A → ⊥) → ⊥) → ⊥) (a : A) . x ((λ h : A → ⊥) . ha) :
((A → ⊥) → ⊥) → ⊥) → (A → ⊥)
$$

### Exercise 1.16

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-1.16">
Show that addition of natural numbers is commutative:
<p class="equation">
$$
\prod\limits_{i,j : \mathbb{N}}\ (i + j = j + i).
$$
</p>
</div>

Hint: by induction twice.

<pre class="Agda">{% raw %}<a id="20880" class="Keyword">module</a> <a id="Ex1-16" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#Ex1-16" class="Module">Ex1-16</a> <a id="20894" class="Keyword">where</a>
  <a id="20902" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="20907" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def" class="Module">ℕ-Def</a>
  <a id="20915" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="20920" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Ind" class="Module">ℕ-Ind</a>
  <a id="20928" class="Keyword">open</a> <a id="20933" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#Ex1-8" class="Module">Ex1-8</a> <a id="20939" class="Keyword">using</a> <a id="20945" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20946" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#Ex1-8._%2B_" class="Function Operator">_+_</a><a id="20949" class="Symbol">)</a>

  <a id="Ex1-16.proof" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#Ex1-16.proof" class="Function">proof</a> <a id="20960" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="20962" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="20963" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20963" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="20965" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="20967" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a><a id="20968" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="20970" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="20972" class="Symbol">((</a><a id="20974" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20974" class="Bound">j</a> <a id="20976" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="20978" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a><a id="20979" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="20981" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="20983" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20963" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="20985" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#Ex1-8._%2B_" class="Function Operator">+</a> <a id="20987" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20974" class="Bound">j</a> <a id="20989" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="20991" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20974" class="Bound">j</a> <a id="20993" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#Ex1-8._%2B_" class="Function Operator">+</a> <a id="20995" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#20963" class="Bound">i</a><a id="20996" class="Symbol">)</a>

    <a id="21012" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Ind.ind" class="Function">ind</a> <a id="21016" class="Symbol">(λ</a> <a id="21019" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="21020" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21020" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="21022" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="21024" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a><a id="21025" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="21027" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="21029" class="Symbol">((</a><a id="21031" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21031" class="Bound">j</a> <a id="21033" class="Symbol">:</a> <a id="21035" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%E2%84%95-Def.%E2%84%95" class="Datatype">ℕ</a><a id="21036" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="21038" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="21040" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21020" class="Bound">i</a> <a id="21042" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#Ex1-8._%2B_" class="Function Operator">+</a> <a id="21044" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21031" class="Bound">j</a> <a id="21046" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="21048" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21031" class="Bound">j</a> <a id="21050" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#Ex1-8._%2B_" class="Function Operator">+</a> <a id="21052" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21020" class="Bound">i</a><a id="21053" class="Symbol">))</a>
      <a id="21062" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21100" class="Function">sproof₁</a>
      <a id="21076" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#21261" class="Function">sproof₂</a>

## Chapter 2

### Exercise 2.6

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.6">
Prove that if $$p : x \equiv y$$, then the function
$$(p \cdot -) : (y \equiv z) \to (x \equiv z)$$ is an equivalence.
</div>

![path-triangle](/assets/ipe-images/path-triangle.png)

<div class="proof">
Solution. <br/>

To show the equivalence, it sufficies to show a function
$$g : x \equiv z \to y \equiv z$$ such that we can prove
$$ (p \cdot -) \circ g \sim \mathsf{id}_{x \equiv z}$$ and
$$ g \circ (p \cdot -) \sim \mathsf{id}_{y \equiv z}$$.

Let's define the function $$g$$.
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
&g : x ≡ z → y ≡ z\\
&g~m~=~\mathsf{trans}~(\mathsf{sym}~p)~m
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
<br/>

($$(p \cdot -) \circ g \sim \mathsf{id}_{x \equiv z}$$):
Let be $$m : x ≡ z$$, we have,

<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
(p \cdot -) \circ g (m) &= (p \cdot -)~(g~m)\\
                        &= (p \cdot -)~(\mathsf{trans}~(\mathsf{sym}~p)~m)\\
                        &= \mathsf{trans}~p~(\mathsf{trans}~(\mathsf{sym}~p)~m)\\
                        &= \mathsf{trans}~(\mathsf{trans}~p~(\mathsf{sym}~p))~m\\
                        &= \mathsf{trans}~\mathsf{refl}_{x≡z}~m\\
                        &= m
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
<br/>
($$ g \circ (p \cdot -) \sim \mathsf{id}_{y \equiv z}$$):
Let be $$n : y ≡ z$$, we have,

<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
g \circ (p \cdot -) n &= g (\mathsf{trans}~p~n)\\
                      &= (\mathsf{trans}~(\mathsf{sym}~p)~(\mathsf{trans}~p~n)\\
                      &= \mathsf{trans}~(\mathsf{trans}~(\mathsf{sym}~p)~p)~n\\
                      &= \mathsf{trans}~\mathsf{refl}_{y ≡ z}~n\\
                      &= n.
\end{align*}
$$
</p>

</div>


### Exercise 2.10

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.10">
Prove that ∑-types are associative, in that for any $$A : \mathcal{U}$$
and families $$B : A  \to U$$ and $$C : \sum_{(x : A)} B(x) \to \mathcal{U}$$,
we have
<p class="equation">
$$\sum\limits_{(x : A)} \sum\limits_{(y : B(x))} C((x,y)) \simeq \sum\limits_{p : \sum_{x:A} B(x)} C(p)$$.
</p>
</div>

<div class="proof" id="proof-2.10">
Solution.<br/>
We can prove that the following functions $$f$$ and $$g$$ are inverses.

<p class="equation">
$$\sum\limits_{(x : A)} \sum\limits_{(y : B(x))} C((x,y)) \overset{f}{\underset{g}{\rightleftarrows}} \sum\limits_{p : \sum_{x:A} B(x)} C(p)$$.
</p>
defined by $$f(a,b,c) :\equiv ((a,b),c)$$ and $$g(z,c) :\equiv (\mathsf{proj}_1 z,\mathsf{proj}_{2} z, c)$$.<br/>
Indeed,
<p class="equation">
$$
\begin{align*}
(f \circ g) (z, c) &:\equiv f (g (z,c))\\
&:\equiv f\,(\mathsf{proj}_1 z,\mathsf{proj}_{2} z, c)\\
&:\equiv ((\mathsf{proj}_1 z,\mathsf{proj}_{2} z), c)
\end{align*}
$$
</p>
</div>

        <a id="25034" class="Symbol">→</a> <a id="25036" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Fun%E2%82%81.g" class="Function">g</a> <a id="25038" class="Symbol">{</a><a id="25039" class="Argument">A</a> <a id="25041" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="25043" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#24931" class="Bound">A</a><a id="25044" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="25046" class="Argument">B</a> <a id="25048" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="25050" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#24941" class="Bound">B</a><a id="25051" class="Symbol">}{</a><a id="25053" class="Argument">C</a> <a id="25055" class="Symbol">=</a> <a id="25057" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#24955" class="Bound">C</a><a id="25058" class="Symbol">}</a> <a id="25060" class="Symbol">(</a><a id="25061" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#%CE%A3-Fun%E2%82%81.f" class="Function">f</a> <a id="25063" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#24983" class="Bound">x</a><a id="25064" class="Symbol">)</a> <a id="25066" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#_%E2%89%A1_" class="Datatype Operator">≡</a> <a id="25068" href="{% endraw %}{% link _posts/2018-04-08-hott-exercises.md %}{% raw %}#24983" class="Bound">x</a>

### Exercise 2.13

<div class="exercise" id="exercise-2.13">
Show that $$(2 \simeq 2) \simeq 2$$.
</div>

<div class="proof" markdown="1">
Solution.<br/>

The following text is from [jdoughertyii](https://github.com/jdoughertyii/hott-exercises/blob/master/Ch02.v).<br/>
The result essentially says that $$2$$ is equivalent to itself in two ways:
the identity provides one equivalence, and negation gives the other.  So we
first define these.  $$\mathsf{id}_{2}$$ is its own quasi-inverse; we have
$$\mathsf{id}_{2} \circ \mathsf{id}_{2} \equiv \mathsf{id}_{2}$$, so $$\mathsf{id}_{2}
\circ \mathsf{id}_{2}
\sim \mathsf{id}_{2}$$ easily.  $$\lnot$$ is also its own quasi-inverse, since for
any $$x$$, $$\lnot\lnot x = x$$.
To show the result, we need to map $$\mathsf{id}_{2}$$ and $$\lnot$$ onto $$2$$ is
a quasi-invertible way.  But we need to define this map on all of $$2
\simeq 2$$.  So for any $$h : 2\simeq 2$$, let $$f(h) = h(0_{2})$$,
and define $$g : 2 \to (2 \simeq 2)$$ by

$$
  g(0_{2}) = \mathsf{id}_{2}
  \qquad\qquad
  g(1_{2}) = \lnot
$$

To show that these are quasi-inverses,
note first that whatever else is the case, an equivalence
$$2 \simeq 2$$ can't be a constant function, which we can prove by a case
analysis.  Each of $$f(0_{2})$$ and $$f(1_{2})$$ is in $$2$$, so it is
either $$0_{2}$$ or $$1_{2}$$.  So we have the cases:
 - $$f(0_{2}) = f(1_{2})$$, in which case we can apply $$f^{-1}$$ to either side to get a contradiction, or
 - $$f(0_{2}) = \lnot f(1_{2})$$. In which case we have the result
Showing that $$f \circ g \sim \mathsf{id}_{2}$$ is easy, since we can do it by
cases.  We have

$$\begin{align*}
  f(g(0_{2})) &= f(\mathsf{id}_{2}) = \mathsf{id}_{2}(0_{2}) = 0_{2}
  \\
  f(g(1_{2})) &= f(\lnot) = \lnot 0_{2} = 1_{2}
\end{align*}%
$$

For the other direction, suppose that $$h : 2 \simeq 2$$ and that
function extensionality holds.
$$h(0_{2})$$ is either $$0_{2}$$ or $$1_{2}$$.  If the first, then
because $$h$$ isn't constant we have $$h(1_{2}) = \lnot h(0_{2}) =
1_{2}$$, hence $$h = \mathsf{id}_{2}$$.  Furthermore,
$$
  g(f(h)) = g(h(0_{2})) = g(0_{2}) = \mathsf{id}_{2} = h
$$
The same argument works for the other case.  So $$f$$ is an equivalence, and
$$(2 \simeq 2) \simeq 2$$.

</div>

### Exercise 2.14

<div class="exercise">

  Suppose we add to type theory <a
  href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IlfQjWqrK6I">the equality reflection
  rule</a> which says that if there is an element $$p : \mathsf{Id}(x,y) $$,
  then in fact $$ x :\equiv y$$. Prove that for any $$p : \mathsf{Id}(x,x)$$ we
  have $$p :\equiv \mathsf{refl}_x$$.

  <p class="equation">
  $$
    \begin{prooftree}
    \AxiomC{$\vdash p : \mathsf{Id}(x, y)$}
    \RightLabel{$\mathsf{Eq}$}
    \UnaryInfC{$\vdash x \equiv y.$}
    \end{prooftree}
  $$
  </p>

</div>

<div class="proof">
  Proof.<br/>
  We first fix the type of $$\mathsf{refl}_x$$ in order to apply effectively
  path induction.<br/>

  <p class="equation">
    $$
    \begin{prooftree}
    \AxiomC{$x : A, y : A, p : x = y ⊢ p : x = y$}
    \RightLabel{$\mathsf{Eq}$}
    \UnaryInfC{$x : A, y : A, p : x = y ⊢ x ≡ y$}
    \AxiomC{$x : A, y : A, p : x = y ⊢ \mathsf{refl}_x : x = x$}
    \BinaryInfC{$x : A, y : A, p : x = y ⊢ \mathsf{refl}_x : x = y.$}
    \end{prooftree}
    $$
  </p>

  Now, $$\mathsf{refl}_x$$ and $$p : x = y$$ in the formulation of path induction
  is well-typed. Therefore, by path induction, we show that
  $$\mathsf{Id}(p,\mathsf{refl_{x}})$$. Let be $$x : A$$ and $$C :\equiv
  \prod_{y : A} \prod_{p : x \equiv y }\ p \equiv \mathsf{refl}_{x}$$.
  It sufficies to show and inhabitant of $$C(x, \mathsf{refl}_{x})$$, and it is,
  $$\mathsf{refl}_{\mathsf{refl}_x} : \mathsf{refl}_x = \mathsf{refl}_x$$.
  By equation reflection rule, since we have an inhabitant of $$p \equiv
  \mathsf{refl}_x$$, these are judgemental equal,i.e., $$p \equiv \mathsf{refl}_x$$.
</div>

### Exercise 2.17

<div class="exercise">
<ul>
  <li> Show that if $$A \simeq A$$  and $$B \simeq B'$$, then $$(A\times B) \simeq (A'\times B')$$. </li>
  <li> Give two proofs of this fact, one using univalence and one not using it, and show that the two proofs are equal.</li>
  <li> Formulate and prove analogous results for the other type formers: $$\Sigma$$, $$\to$$, $$\Pi$$, and $$+$$. </li>
</ul>
</div>

<div class="proof" markdown="1">
- Assuming univalence.
<br/>
$$
\begin{prooftree}
\AxiomC{$f : A \simeq A$}
\RightLabel{$\mathsf{ua}$}
\UnaryInfC{$A =_{\mathcal{U}} A$}
\AxiomC{$g : B \simeq B'$}
\RightLabel{$\mathsf{ua}$}
\UnaryInfC{$B =_{\mathcal{U}} B'$}
\RightLabel{$\mathsf{pair=}$}
\BinaryInfC{$(A\times B) =_{\mathcal{U}} (A'\times B')$}
\RightLabel{$\mathsf{idtoequiv}$}
\UnaryInfC{$(A\times B) \simeq (A'\times B')$}
\end{prooftree}
$$

- Without using univalence, it is easy to prove
that the function $$h$$ defined as follows gives us the
equivalence that we are looking for.

$$
\begin{align*}
&h : (A\times B) \to (A'\times B')\\
&h (a , b) = (f\, a, g\, b).
\end{align*}
$$

With the inverse:

$$
\begin{align*}
&h^{-1} : (A'\times B') \to (A\times B)\\
&h^{-1} (a , b) = (f^{-1}\, a, g^{-1}\, b).
\end{align*}
$$

To prove these proofs are equal it is sufficies to
show these underlyding functions are equal.


</div>

## Chapter 3

To solve the following exercises, let us recall a few things:

- The *set* definition in HoTT:

A type $$A$$ is a **set** if for all $$x, y : A$$ and
all $$p, q : x \equiv y$$, we have $$ p \equiv q$$. In a proposition
we have

$$
\mathsf{isSet}(A) :\equiv \prod\limits_{(x,y : A)}\prod\limits_{(p,q : x \equiv y)} (p \equiv q).
$$

- The type for equivalence from $$A$$ to $$B$$

$$
  (A \simeq B) :\equiv \sum\limits_{f : A \to B} \mathsf{isequiv}(f),
$$

where

$$
\mathsf{isequiv(f)} :\equiv
  \left (\sum\limits_{g : B \to A} (f \circ g \sim \mathsf{id}_{B})\right) \times
  \left (\sum\limits_{h : B \to A} (h \circ f \sim \mathsf{id}_{A})\right)
$$

- The homotopy concept:

Let $$f , g : \prod\limits_{(x:A)} P(x)$$ be two sections of a
type family $$P : A \to \mathcal{U}$$. A **homotopy** from $$f$$ to $$g$$
is a dependent function of type

$$
(f \sim g) :\equiv \prod\limits_{x : A} (f(x) \equiv g(x)).
$$

### Exercise 3.1

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$A\simeq B$$ and $$A$$ is a set, then so is $$B$$.
</div>


<div class="proof" id="proof-3.1">
Proof 1.<br/>
Let be $$x,y : B$$ and $$p : x \equiv_{B} y$$ and $$q : x \equiv_{B} y$$.
We need to prove $$ p \equiv q$$.<br/>
Since $$A\simeq B$$ then there is a function $$f : A \to B$$ and some
$$g : B \to A$$ such that $$f \circ g \sim id_{B}$$.
Using this function $$g$$ over the path $$p$$ we get
$$\mathsf{ap}_{g} p : g x \equiv_{A} g y$$.
We do the same but this time over the path $$q$$, that is,
$$\mathsf{ap}_{g} q : g x \equiv_{A} g y$$.
Because of $$A$$ is a set, we have a new path called
$$m :\mathsf{ap}_{g} p \equiv_{gx \equiv_{A} gy} \mathsf{ap}_{g} q$$. <br/>

Now, an action over this path $$m$$
using the function $$\mathsf{ap}_{f} : x \equiv_{A} y \to f x \equiv_{B} f y$$
will give us


$$
\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{ap}_{f}} m :
(\mathsf{ap}_{f}) (\mathsf{ap}_{g} p) \equiv (\mathsf{ap}_{f})  (\mathsf{ap}_{g} q).
$$


By the lemmas in Chapter 2, we do the following reasoning:

$$
\begin{align*}
(\mathsf{ap}_{f}) (\mathsf{ap}_{g} p) \equiv (\mathsf{ap}_{f})  (\mathsf{ap}_{g} q) &=
  \mathsf{ap}_{f \circ g} p \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{f \circ g} q\\
  &=(\text{transporting by using} f \sim g)\\
  &=\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{id}_{B}} p \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{id}_{B}} q\\
  &=p \equiv q.
\end{align*}
$$

Then, we have the inhabitant, $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{ap}_{f}} m : p \equiv q$$.
</div>

### Exercise 3.2

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$A$$ and $$B$$ are sets, then so is $$A+B$$.
</div>

To solve this exercise, we should take a look of some results from Chapter 2,
Section 2.12.

<div class="proof" id="proof-3.2" markdown="1">
Proof.<br/>

Let be $$x, y : A + B$$, and paths $$p : x \equiv y$$, $$q : x \equiv
y$$. Let's get a path $$p \equiv q$$.  We proceed by case analysis. If
$$x :\equiv \mathsf{inl} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inl} b$$, for
some $$a, b : A$$ then $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p : a
\equiv_{A} b$$ and $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q : a \equiv_{A}
b$$.

Since $$A$$ is a set, there is a path between these last two terms,
this is, $$m : \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p \equiv
\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q$$.  Now, an action over this path
$$m$$ using the $$\mathsf{inl}$$ function give us:
$$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}} m : \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p) \equiv \mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} q)$$.<br/>

By path algebra we have $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
m : p \equiv q$$ since $$\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}}
(\mathsf{ap}_{\mathsf{inl}^{-1}} p) \equiv p$$.<br/> Following the
same reasoning, we prove the case $$x :\equiv \mathsf{inr} a$$ and $$y
:\equiv \mathsf{inr} b$$.  For the latest cases, $$x :\equiv
\mathsf{inl} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inr} b$$ and $$x :\equiv
\mathsf{inr} a$$ and $$y :\equiv \mathsf{inl} b$$, we use the
encode-decode method to derive a proof term for 𝟘 from
$$p$$ and $$q$$. Then, we may conclude anything we wish, that is, $$p
\equiv q$$.
</div>


### Exercise 3.3

<div class="exercise">
Prove that if $$ A $$ is a set and $$B : A \to \mathcal{U}$$
is a type family such that $$B(x)$$ is a set for all
$$x : A$$, then $$\Sigma\limits_{(x:A)}\ B(x)$$ is a set.
</div>

MISSING.

### Exercise 3.4

<div class="exercise">
Show that $$A$$ is a mere proposition if and only
if $$A\to A$$ is contractible.
</div>

<div class="proof" markdown="1">
Proof. <br/>
- We must to show an inhabitant of the following type:

$$
\mathsf{isProp}(A) \to \sum\limits_{f : A \to A}\, \prod\limits_{g : A \to A } f = g.
$$

This is my proposed term:

$$
t :\equiv λ \mathsf{Aprop} \to (\mathsf{id}_{A}, λ (g : A \to A) \to \mathsf{funext} (\lambda (x : A) \to \mathsf{Aprop}~(\mathsf{id}~x)~(g~x)).
$$

- If $$A → A$$ is contractible, all functions in this type are equal,
then in particular given $$x, y : A$$, the constant functions $$f(w) \equiv x$$
and $$g(w) \equiv y$$ are equal. Then, $$\mathsf{happly} (f =_{A \to A} g, w) : x = y$$.
Therefore $$A$$ is a mere proposition.

</div>
